et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	"If the fistula is very deep in its direct course, you must cut deeply into it as far as you can,"
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	"then insert moistened probes dipped in hot medicine and push them up to the head of the fistula;"
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	"until the medicine corrodes all the excess tissue that remains at the bottom."
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"And then apply warm applications of clean, healing liniments until it is healed;"
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	"If it does not heal with these methods, cauterize it as we have said;"
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	"And if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut into it."
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	"If a vein or nerve troubles you in the main members, as we have said,"
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	"And if bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it away until all the corruption is removed;"
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	"then treat it with warm applications of clean, healing liniments until it is healed."
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	"If it does not heal and again becomes inflamed as before,"
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	"know that you have not yet reached the bottom:"
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	"So uncover and probe until you reach the bottom;"
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	"And remove all the corruption, then dress it properly."
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	"and if it is healed in this way, that's good."
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	"But if not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;"
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	"So there is no other remedy than leaving it alone to nature:"
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	"And if there is a small piece of corrupted bone that you can grasp with forceps,"
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	"remove it with an appropriate instrument;"
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	"And if there are many pieces of bone, crush them all finely and leave not one behind;"
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	"If moisture opposes you, and there is no mistake or fear,"
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	"then cut through flesh, moisture, and bone, and free the bones."
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	"And if you cannot remove them at once, apply a warm poultice to absorb corruption;"
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	"and leave it until the surrounding area is softened;"
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	"then they will be easier to remove."
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	"And if it is a large bone, such as in the thigh or leg,"
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	"scrape off only the corruption until all blackness is removed;"
puis restoure la plaie;	"then dress the wound."
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	"And if there is much corrupted flesh reaching up to the bone,"
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	"It must be scraped down to the corruption and then treated until it is solid;"
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	"I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg,"
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	So that you may take example and aid from this in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg caused by something that entered his body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	Until the matter came to the leg,
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	"But physicians through their folly operated so much upon him that they opened up the abscesses."
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	"and as they scraped away many materials, it turned into a fistula, and there came many openings that all poured out bowels and moisture from the body."
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	"And for about two years many physicians treated him, but there was no skilled surgeon among them,"
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	"So I was called in, and saw his leg and the medications they were treating him with,"
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	"And what ran through the openings was great corruption."
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	"And the young man's skin became red, and he had a lemon-colored hue."
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	"I applied a poultice to one of these openings, and then searched for all the openings,"
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	"and found that they were connected to each other throughout the whole leg."
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	"I therefore hurried and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a portion of the bone,"
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	"and found it rotten and penetrated by corruption which had reached the bone inside."
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	"I removed what appeared to me of the rotted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption besides what I had taken out,"
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	"And began to dress the wound with dry medicines for a long time, but could not heal it."
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	"Then I reopened and again discovered the bone as before,"
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	"And found that the corruption had continued into the bone, and scraped it away and removed it, and then tried to heal the wound."
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	"But I could not do so until I cut around about a palm's width of bone and completely removed it."
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	"Then I dressed it with medicines, and he was soon healed and soundly."
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	"And there was no need to reopen the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not tolerate,"
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	"and because of my fear that he might die."
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	"For after the evacuation of blood he often swooned, but nevertheless he was entirely healed,"
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	"And in the place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was in good condition and suffered neither harm nor disadvantage at any time thereafter."
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	"And if the bone is broken anywhere else in the body, it should be treated as follows:"
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	"Take one linen cloth, and bind it around the head of the exposed bone,"
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	"and command him to stretch it upwards;"
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	"And put another thicker linen band on top of the first one, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone,"
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	"And stretch out the head so that you can pull out the rotted flesh underneath,"
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	"And uncover the flesh where you want to see it, so that the bone does not blanch the flesh."
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	"And put a hot ember or a red-hot iron under the bone to burn away the rotted flesh;"
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	"And this must be done until one can see and feel that the rottenness is gone, and it must still be repeated."
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	"If the bone itself is rotten and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,"
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	"then uncover all the flesh; then put a hot ember underneath,"
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	"and then scrape away the corruption from one part to the other with an iron that is as long as the corruption itself, as we have said;"
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	"And if the corruption is in a joint, cut away the rotted joint and scrape the bone that it contains from the other side,"
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	"If the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then there is no other choice but to cut it away."
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	"And if the corruption is at the palm of the hand or the sole of the foot, that is very serious indeed,"
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	"But nonetheless you must inquire how this corruption opens up,"
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	"And clean it in every way that you can, but make sure that the veins or nerves do not get in your way;"
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	"and know that there are many types of incisions and irons for cutting these bones according to their position and appearance,"
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	"according to their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;"
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	"And therefore it is necessary to equip each type of bone with its appropriate instrument."
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	"And know that this work will show you the instrument that you will need according to your knowledge of this art,"
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	"and the testimony of the ways in which diseases occur;"
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	"So consider the instrument that you need according to what is appropriate for it."
dou feu	"from fire"
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	"The flesh decays either due to an internal cause or due to a lack of something."
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	"And when you have treated that corruption with medicinal cures and they do not help,"
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	"then it is necessary to cut off that member until the place where the corruption begins,"
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	"So that the sick person escapes from death through this means, or at least avoids the greater harm of losing a limb."
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	"And the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if it had been burnt by fire,"
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	"and after this blackness comes corruption of limb after limb,"
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	"And spreads throughout the body; so hurry to cut it off,"
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	"If it is due to the sting of some venomous creatures such as scorpions, vipers and similar ones,"
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	"if the corruption is at the top of the thigh, cut it off, without letting it come close to the hand."
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	"And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it off at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm;"
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	"And if it reaches the arm, cut it off at the elbow; and if it goes beyond the elbow, that is death."
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	"There are no remedies that can help other than those of great power;"
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	"And the same applies when corruption reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut it off after the next joint;"
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	"And if it comes to the ankle, cut off the whole foot."
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	"And if it reaches the leg, cut off at the knee joint;"
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	"And if it goes above the knee, there is no other option but to let the sick person die."
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	"The manner of cutting off or sewing up the member is that you tie it above and below,"
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	"And extend some assistants one towards the lower tie, and others towards the upper one,"
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	"And cut open the flesh between the two ties with a wide spatula until the bone is exposed;"
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	"then cut it off or sew it up, and place on each side a linen cloth so that the suture does not touch the healthy area,"
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	"And come to the sick person's other wounds and ulcers."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	"And if bleeding occurs while you are operating, cauterize it immediately,"
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	"or put on some constricting powders. Then return to your treatment until it is completed."
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	"Then tie the wounded member with a suitable bandage and treat it until it heals;"
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	"And I will tell you what happened to one man in sumpter:"
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	"He had a blackness that seemed like being burnt by fire,"
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	"And this corruption first appeared on his foot's big toe and spread to affect the whole foot;"
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	"But when the man saw the corruption, he quickly cut off his foot and was healed."
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	"And some time later the corruption returned to the big toe of his hand, and he came to me,"
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	"I put on things that reflected heat after cleansing his body, but the corruption could not be stopped;"
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	"But he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I refused because I hoped to drive back the material;"
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	"And I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die."
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	"because the man's strength was weak; and he became completely discouraged and returned home,"
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	"And he quickly cut off his hand and was healed."
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	"And I have told you this story only so that others may learn from it what to do if they are ever in need."
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	"Sometimes an ulcer appears in a fleshy area and lasts so long that it attracts many flies;"
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	"And then it becomes round and hollows out, and the flies jump into it and leave the area empty like a vessel."
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	"And the skin that is above it is as thin as delicate silk;"
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	"But it does not go down to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called 'healthy.'"
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	"And is not called a fistula."
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	"But if it extends so far that it reaches the bone inside, then it is called a fistula;"
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	"And the skin is such that you must cut all around it, especially if it is thin like silk;"
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	"And do not be afraid of its corruption."
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	"But if you think that the skin is dangerous and the corruption is not deep,"
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And the hide is thick with flesh; thus treat it with an enema:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look if the breast is large and the bowel that comes out has a foul odor
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then apply an Egyptian suppository made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take equal parts of senna, oil, and litharge, and put them in a vessel on the fire
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	Then take some according to your need, and mix it with water and honey
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and insert the suppository into the anus, and close the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	Let the medicine remain there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing it out
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this as many times as necessary until the breast is softened and the foul odor is gone
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and once anointed with water containing ashes
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	When this medicine is not present and you take ashes from vine wood and pour water over them
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it and apply it as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	And if the patient cannot tolerate this or if the Egyptian suppository or water containing ashes
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	Then use an enema of water and honey with a little crushed litharge in it
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	Or you may use an enema made from melted honey and wine that has the property to cleanse and wash
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this and are confident that the breast is well cleansed
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then apply an enema made from those things which cause flesh to form in it
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	Take diaphoretic plaster and make a poultice with rose oil and wine
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or use other medicines and oils of which I have spoken their properties when treating oils
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	And if the opening of the breast is small and the tube for the enema cannot be inserted
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then dilate it slightly with an iron and insert a tampon soaked in Egyptian ointment
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, then apply a stitch and leave it only for one hour so that the enema can be inserted
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the opening that secretes milk is above, then make an incision somewhat lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the breast is deep, do not let flesh grow in it
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot close the wound underneath as you see it
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then prepare it in such a way that the breast is directed towards the lowest point where it is.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the breast is deep, do not let flesh grow into it
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot close up underneath as you see it
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then prepare it in such a way that the breast slopes slightly downward and do not leave any part of the breast protruding
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	Take medicines that strengthen to apply on the breast
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and lay over it one cloth made of linen which covers the whole breast.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	Then close up tightly around the opening of the breast, about a little larger than the first one
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	Then apply soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it over the opening of the breast to support the breast and do not remove the large cloth outside until after many days once
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And the one on the opening of the breast is removed often in order to remove the milk.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	Know what comes out of the breast, whether it is venom or little or enough, whether digested or undigested
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	Take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	And when your treatment has extended in this way and you see that the milk begins to flow from the opening of the breast
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is beginning to heal and the health is approaching.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	And then remove it in the morning or on the third day, and when you remove the wound
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change another cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if after many days the breast continues to secrete undigested milk, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come out after a long time, do not despair of the health
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For health is approaching. For there are men for whom it takes a long time for flesh to grow in their wounds and others who have the opposite condition.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested milk flows from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the breast takes a long time to heal and is prolapsed, apply drying medicines in substance and in power.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphoretic ointment, for there is a large part of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphoretic ointment, made with rose oil, and rise it with old wine equal in substance
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and this is better cooked until thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When diaphoretic ointments are not available
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and powder them onto the honey while it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	And then apply a cloth, one draught, to it, and stretch it over the breast; sometimes an astrologer long is administered there
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is also like wheat flour and oatmeal
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And in the case of simple or composite herbs: grind them up, make them into powder, and apply honey as mentioned above
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this treatment
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	Then know that the corruption has penetrated deeply, causing pressure on the bone, or in hard members, or in joints
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If it is a fistula cure, as we said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil of the toe
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is a boil that arises under the nail of the thumb of the hand
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or sometimes it appears on other toes
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	And when it is neglected and not taken care of, a large boil forms there
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and spread so much that they reach the root of the nail, sometimes even entirely consuming it
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corruption reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain; the skin of the toe is swollen and reddened in color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have described in that section, but the treatment does not help
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	Then you must cut off about a third of the nail with iron tongs, removing all the excess
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is greatly beneficial if the bone and the nail are healthy
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the flesh and starts to throb and become inflamed
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must put the root of the plantain under the nail where the flesh is pointing
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and bring it upwards, and cut off that tender and delicate flesh gently
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply burning and corrosive medications to the remaining flesh to remove all of it
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply hot fomentations until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption has reached the bone, cut it out and cauterize the wound, for as long as the bone remains corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see that the toe is rotting, then cut it off with iron tongs as described earlier
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it becomes gangrenous and putrid, causing great pain, then you must first cleanse it
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then cut the nail of the big toe with the sharp edge of the scissors across the top
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel great pain
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, apply something to ease the pain
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of gout in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Some men have toes that are very fatty in their hands
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone or even nail present
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them grow at the root of the joint or on one of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born with a knot of the two does not move
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the joint of the two sometimes moves
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of one who is fleshly is light in this way
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	waist to its root by a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure, so he should hold onto the cover
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or has a knot in the hind part of the joint, it is necessary to first cut around the flesh up to the bone
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then cure it until it is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sinews that come together at the two joints come by birth, or by the union of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary to cut this union so that the limbs return according to their natural shapes;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	"Then place between two tents or cloths moistened with rosewater oil, so they do not adhere."
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you place between two pieces of thin lead until the joint is well seated, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling occurs on either side with the palm, scrape away this scurf as needed.
Des vils	Of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Wounds are swollen, large blisters filled with melancholic excess matter that come from many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And they happen more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him a laxative for the colon, and then the holy water of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure with iron is done in two ways: one is to cut it and draw out the black blood from the wound;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is to lift the blister and draw out all its contents.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cauterization should be done in this manner: first, raise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the large blood is subtilized;
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strap the sick leg from above the hip down to below the knee joint;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the blister in one place or two or three with a wide cauterization tool;
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then remove and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's virtue can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then wash it off, and command that they bind him tightly with flesh-colored bandages around his blackened neck;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin again the evacuation and cleansing when the vessels are full, for it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of the limb is done in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then place it in a bath and pour hot water over the leg until it turns red and swells the vessels;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, then heat it by the fire, and then wrap it around near the vessel of the long bone at the top of the knee or below at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with an awl and strip back the vessel from each side until it becomes apparent when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the probe underneath until it raises the vessel from the skin, and then pierce it lightly with an awl
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then place a second compress three fingers away from the first one, then strip back the skin over the vessel until it becomes visible
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then raise it with your finger, just as you did before, and pierce it with another awl in the same manner
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then place another compress or several if needed, then raise it again and secure it at the two ends of the foot
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then traction and elevation until you reach the second compress, then extract it compress by compress until it comes out entirely, then secure it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot traction and elevate it, then insert a strong doubled thread needle into the vessel
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it off and traction it, and place your finger underneath, turning your hand back and forth until it comes out entirely.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be sure that it does not slip away because if it does slip away then you cannot traction or elevate it and harm will come to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have completely extracted it, then place on the wound area wool moistened with wine and rose oil, and let it soak until it is clean.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vessel is contracted, twisted, and coiled together, and not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that you cut it incorrectly, but do not cover it; and draw it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one covers the screw is curved, and it does not cut, so that it covers the thread.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	"If it were thin, it would block the vein, but let it be thick as we have said; this is the form:"
De la voinne civile	Of civil war
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is inserted into legs, warm regions where no herbs or trees grow, and in land with no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to rot that originates beneath the skin
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	like when it enters the body like serpents and worms, inserted between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the sign that this vein has begun is that there is a very great inflammation in the leg
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the location changes and the vein begins to emerge from its hiding place, like a plant's root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the flesh opens, you must wrap around it a piece of linen two and a half fingers wide up to two fingers, and knot
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the linen hanging on the leg; whenever blood flows out again, wrap the linen around it and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it's too long, cut off part of it, wrap the remaining piece around it, but do not cut its root until it has all emerged.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will retreat into the flesh and cause an abscess and rot at that location, leading to a bad illness
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, it must be treated gradually until its head appears and none remains in the body
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein is as long as five palms or ten
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man once came to me whose vein was twenty palms long; when you cut it, it will gush out one quart or more, and pierce all the way through to its depth
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	until all of it comes out; then empty the matter inside and apply medicine at that location to prevent rot for a few days before treating it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it opens in the ankle of the foot or on the foot itself
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there are many holes from which blood flows; therefore treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Concerning worms that arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cattle sickness," because it often occurs among oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	"And there exists a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, traveling up and down throughout the body,"
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	"and it can be felt well as it travels from limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes away;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	"And it is caused by putrefaction of certain humours, such as come worms and serpents, and tapeworms, and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	"And its harmfulness is doubted, for when it travels through the body and ascends to the head, it reaches the eye,"
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	"perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; this happens many times."
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	"When you see one being cleaned and drawn out, then one can only perceive it when it moves:"
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	"So it is necessary that you tie the wound above and below with a strong thread, very tightly,"
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	"then cut on top of it and draw it out, and if the worm has burrowed deeply into the flesh and you do not find it,"
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	"then cauterize it with fire until it dies;"
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	"And the greatest harm that it causes is that it blinds the eye, as we have said;"
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	"But if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, press down on the eyebrow tightly below it, then cut above and draw it out;"
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	"And it is necessary to use the remedy of purification of the body with dissolving medicines for putrid humours,"
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	"and beware of eating decaying meats."
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	On the Pain That Comes from Flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	"This disease is called in our land 'wakiir' and is a pain that occurs in certain limbs,"
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	"and then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you."
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	"I was summoned to see an ill woman, and when I examined her arm, I saw a small swelling in the armpit;"
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	"And shortly afterward, she saw something like a worm rising to the shoulder,"
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	"more quickly than anything else, as if it were quicksilver moving from one place to another;"
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	"The pain moved away from that spot and lodged itself in the shoulder,"
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	"and then shortly thereafter it spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm;"
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	"then she told me that she was continually turning around her body as I saw."
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I was greatly amazed at how she moved from limb to limb in this way, for I had never seen this disease manifest itself like this before."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	"Nevertheless, I had often seen pain move from one place to another,"
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	"But I had never seen it like this before, as I saw in this woman;"
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	"And I thought that perhaps this was because the woman had a dry body and exposed armpits,"
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	"and therefore this constrained wind appeared;"
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	"And it is not seen in those who are delicate and have moist bodies and concealed armpits."
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	"And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have described,"
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	"if the skin above and below rises quickly, and then suddenly contracts so much that the constrained wind breaks out at that spot;"
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	"And cauterize the spot; if you don’t see it with your own eyes,"
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	"then treat it as one would treat windy conditions, such as with fetid pills, pills of saffron, and similar remedies."
Des saiettes	"Regarding hiccups:"
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"The causes of hiccups are varied according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they occur."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	"There are various kinds of hiccups: some have sharp points, others have small ones, some are hairy, and some are smooth;"
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	"and there are those with two angles, those with tongues, and those with fragments;"
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	"And hiccups that occur in any limb do so in one of two ways: either they come from the main limb,"
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	"such as the head, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs."
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	"When hiccups occur in any part of these limbs, and you see the signs of death that I will tell you about later:"
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	"you must beware of extracting this hiccup, for death often follows in many cases;"
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	"And when this bad sign is not apparent and the hiccup is not deep, then treat it and heal the wound."
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	"The sign of hiccups occurring in the head is when they pierce the bone and cause the fontanelle above the brain to bulge out;"
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	"and when there is darkness and dizziness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, inflammation of the tongue and its redness, spasm and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile."
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	"And sometimes there is fluid from the nose or ears; sometimes speech and voice are lost;"
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	"and there suddenly appears moist white flesh resembling that of chickens, and also burning like raw flesh;"
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	"And if this sign is apparent to you, then beware of treating it; extract the hiccup only if it is not inside."
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	"The signs that hiccups occur in the heart are when they are close to the left nipple and feel as if they were stuck in something hard, not empty;"
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	"And sometimes hiccups move like those of chickens, and there is black blood; coldness and cold sweat come on, and syncope occurs;"
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	"then know for certain that death is near."
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The sign of hiccups that occur near the lung is when foamless sputum suddenly comes from the wound; the throat swells up and the patient changes color, sighs loudly, and seeks cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"And if hiccups occur in the covering of the stomach, near the ribs, they cause much belching and great pain with sighing; all the members of the shoulders move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if hiccups occur in the stomach, sometimes undigested meat comes out from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if hiccups occur in the belly and blood flows through the intestines suddenly, there is no hope of recovery or extraction of the hiccup."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if hiccups occur in the bladder and urine suddenly comes out with blood, and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is mortal."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"Other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary muscles, spinal column, buttocks, thighs, and legs, etc., are safe according to many conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When hiccups occur in a nerve or artery and are not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do the same."
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	"It happened to one man that hiccups struck him in the arm at the root of his nose;"
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	"I probed it and extracted it on the other side beneath the ear's fat, without causing any harm."
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	"And I extracted one hiccup that struck in the fat of the eye under its membrane,"
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	"and the hiccup was embedded, and I could hardly touch it except for its tip facing towards the wood;"
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	"And the hiccup was as large as an archer's bowstring, easily extracted without causing any pain or harm to the eye; the man recovered and had no bad consequences."
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	"I extracted a hiccup from a Christian's throat; it was large like an Arabian's ear;"
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	"After shaving his beard, I probed carefully and extracted the hiccup; the Christian recovered."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	"I extracted a hiccup from one man who had it in his belly; I thought he was going to die;"
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	"but after thirty days passed, his condition did not change;"
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	"I cut into the hiccup, extracted it with forceps, and there were no bad consequences."
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	"And once I saw a man whom hiccups struck in the back; the wound had healed on top;"
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	"but the hiccup remained inside him and did not change his natural condition;"
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	"He found no harm in any of his natural works."
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	"I saw another man whom hiccups struck on the face; the wound had healed;"
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	"and it remained inside without causing him great pain; there were many similar cases."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	"I extracted one hiccup from a man of the king's household who had it in his nose;"
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	"And it was somewhat inclined towards the right side, and the hiccup was completely embedded;"
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	"I was called to treat him three days after he was struck; I found the wound very narrow."
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	"I probed it carefully with a delicate probe but could not feel it;"
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	"And he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear."
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	"I thought that it was due to the tip of the hiccup;"
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	"So I applied an attracting plaster on the spot so that the wound would not swell;"
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	"And then the hiccup's head appeared."
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	"I applied the plaster for several days until the wound healed again; the sick man remained thus for a long time;"
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he feels the arrowhead for one day inside his flesh; and he tells you this
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied hot corrosive medication to the wound several times until it healed completely
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I felt around and found the tip of the arrowhead sticking out;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied this hot medication to the wound opening until the tip of the arrowhead was clearly visible
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the healing continued well for four months
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	but then I tore open the wound so that I could insert forceps and pull from both sides, but it would not come out
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	so then I kept experimenting with different methods using various tools until finally, one day, I grabbed it successfully with well-made forceps
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what is described at the end of this chapter, so that I could pull it out and close the wound
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	so I closed it up again, and the wound healed completely, and the patient was entirely cured
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you about the extraction of some arrowheads,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	"Therefore you should rely on what I do not mention, as books cannot cover everything."
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	"But wise teachers compare a few things carefully, including what is present and missing."
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	True work, and nine instruments are needed for the extraction of foreign bodies occurring in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that splinters exit from the limbs where they are inserted only in two ways
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they entered,
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	"and that which jumps out where it enters is an arrow entering flesh, and sometimes jumps out now."
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	"And if it does not jump out now, let it remain until the wound around it closes up, then the joint will be released."
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	"And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it remain like this for a few days, moving it each day."
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	"and then it will jump out; and if it does not jump out, bore all around with a fine needle until the place is widened, then pull it."
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	"And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bone at the top and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain,"
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	"do not pull it out but let it remain until it is healed after a few days,"
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrowhead comes to the brain, it's fatal."
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	"And if the arrowhead is only stuck in the bone and does not reach the brain,"
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	"and after a few days without any bad accident happening to him, prepare to pull it out."
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out, then apply poultices around it as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	"And if the arrowhead is buried in the flesh so that one cannot see it, search for it by touch all around;"
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	"and if you feel it, pull it out with some suitable instrument."
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	"And if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead,"
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	"then cut until the wound is large enough."
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	"And pull out the arrowhead if you can, and if there are barbs on it that hold it in place,"
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	"then cut off the flesh that is stuck into it from two sides as much as you can,"
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	"and then break or bend the barbs of the arrowhead so that you can pull it out."
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	"And be careful not to break the arrowhead while pulling it out, so as not to cause more pain."
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot do it all at once, leave the arrowhead until the wound around it is healed, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	"And if bleeding makes you faint, apply the treatments that we have described in our chapter on wounds."
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	"and beware of cutting into nerves and veins, and devise how you can pull out the arrowhead without danger."
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	"Soon or late, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow struck him,"
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	"for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do it, place him according to the signs that indicate to you how."
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	"The arrowhead that sticks out on the other side and shows through can be pulled out easily,"
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then until the forceps can grasp it, and then pull it out; if now it is burning.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, twist your hand round until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then resume traction until it comes out completely;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the pin of the splint is there, remove the splint from the entire bone
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the bone falls and you see that reduction must be applied, then apply one traction device
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the splint enters into the socket of the traction device; and then pull it out
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the splint is stuck in place, insert one pointed traction device inside to aid with traction
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the splint has been cut, then you must cut all the flesh around where the veins are, if you can
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then dress the wound as it should be dressed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the splint falls on or near the bladder or the belly or the ribs and it is close by and you can cut it off, then do so
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or the nerve, then pull it out and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and care for it until it is healed
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat splints is similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the butt end is also like that of a bird's feather
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to attach to the tip of the arrowhead, as shown here is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pliers for attaching and removing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common flesh
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins that drain are 31, from which there are 16 at the head,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	It is to know: two bat-like structures located after the ears, called the temples "herbich".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins located on either side of each eye called "aspirates".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that runs across the forehead; and the vein at the top of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons located on the neck
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the upper lip of the mouth, which are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And there are two veins beneath the tongue
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The common veins in each arm are five in number
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One of these is the cephalic vein, which runs along the right side of the chest and is commonly called "the vein of the head" by laypeople
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median vein is called "fasta", composed of the cephalic and basilica veins
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and it is commonly called "the heart vein" by laypeople, while the basilica runs along the left side
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the abdominal vein, which is above the forearm bone
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	It is also called the anterior interosseous vein, which is clearly visible in the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The savatella vein is located between the little finger and the ring finger on both sides
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	In the leg and foot, there are three veins:
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second sphenoid bone, which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And there are three veins underneath those on the other leg
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The sacredness of the veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrhs and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the sanctity, as I told you, are such that you should raise the head of the patient
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	Then rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then strap the patient's neck with a vise
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places on the head
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Then grasp them with your two fingers and where you feel the pulse beneath your fingers, then squeeze firmly
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet, and thrust it under the vein up to the bone; then lift your hand all along the upstream vein
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through skin and vein well with two fingers across, and let out blood until you see it
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then bind and tie it, until it is stanched
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said about the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The sanctity of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good against old migraines
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and soda, and customary ophthalmia, and to the course of tears gone astray in the eyes
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the sanctity are such as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient straps their neck so that the two veins appear clearly
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse beneath your fingers and then squeeze firmly
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the skin upwards on the vein with your index finger, and thrust the lancet underneath
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein and cut it, just as you did with the other two veins, and let out blood according to your necessity
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then untie the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then tie it firmly and leave it until it is stanched. And we have already spoken about their cutting and extracting in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The sanctity of the frontal vein is just as valuable as that of the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, migraines, and redness
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its qualities are such that the patient twists their neck until the veins appear
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "the fossor," of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let out blood according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then untie the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is stanched, sometimes with a wide flame
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not necessary for the bandages to be too tight; and tie them diagonally, because the bone is nearby, and by chance the bandage may break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The sanctity of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps with the eyes and with dizziness, redness, inflammation of the eye, and diseases of the face
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And its qualities are such that the patient twists their neck with any kind of tie, as before
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then sanctify it and make the sanctity diagonal, somewhat long and somewhat wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandage is too thin, it may break. Then let out blood according to your necessity and then tie on cotton, tying it tightly
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The sanctity of the nasal vein is beneficial for ague, frenzied soda, and diseases of the face
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	especially for migraines and redness that come in the face, particularly when they are old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And its qualities are such that the patient twists their neck and then holds their nose with your left hand
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a thin long bandage and insert it between the two nostrils in the space that is between them
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not appear well here, and blood will begin to flow now
