et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let out blood according to your necessity, then tie it for one night because it is very quickly restored
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the shape of the bandage:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The sanctity of the two large veins helps with the stretching of the small intestine, the beginning of worms, and many diseases, and with eczema, corrosion, herpetic infections, and eruptions
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And its qualities are such that the patient twists their neck on both sides, as we have said
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing on the head of the patient and the patient sit on a chair
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then sanctify the vein lengthwise somewhat widely and then let out blood temperately or according to necessity
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repeat on the other vein and untie the tie and press gently between the veins
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle themselves. Leave it until morning when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On the sanctity of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sanctity of the veins above the lips helps with coughing in the mouth and with gum corrosion, lip fissures, nosebleeds, and around the nostrils
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And its qualities are such that you make the patient sit in front of you and twist their neck as I have said
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip and look for two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the leftlip
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and recognize them by their black color and by the small dark veins around them
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then sanctify both of them if you cannot recognize them or if you are unsure
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	"Cut off the thickest one from each side,
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healing beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the cephalic vein, and it is at the narrowing of the throat, and with diseases of the eye, and with diseases of the mouth
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the characteristics of the veins are that the patient should raise his hands before the sun, and lift the tongue, and look beneath on each side for a black vein
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then heal one and the other, but do not go too deep, because below are the arteries
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm which are commonly treated are healed in two ways
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with one flame of myrtle or olive oil subtly as with a narrow sword, and it is called "aneasile"
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide or thin according to the width and narrowing of the veins
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the myrtle flame is very well-known, and it is wide as you see
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth and full of thick blood in order to release thick and turbid blood
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed and is for healing thin veins that contain clear yellow blood
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are beneath the throat, neck, cheek, and belly
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the physician to heal it carefully, and to beware of the artery that lies below it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow copiously, then he should press upon it as I have said
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be pointed but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open up clearly, then it is necessary for you to draw it out and change to another one
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or any vein that you want from it, or you heal in its place the vein in the arm: it opens up clearly
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with the flame called "anesile" as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place for healing, then it is also necessary that you draw out the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with incense and then bind the arm and cut the vein with the flame called "anesile"
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not wound the artery when you see the place swell up, for it is of the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see something come out above like urine from a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	then quickly place your finger on top for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which happens many times
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you bind the arm and leave it thus, and do not move it yourself nor let the sick person move it until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and you faint, and there is no physician present, then cut the artery if it is open for the sake of the head; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a fig leaf, slit it open, and take one half and bind it well until the next day
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding has stopped, that is good; if not, then heal it as we have said with powders that stop bleeding
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and stopping the bleeding is not important in many cases for a small wound and the strength of the binding on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein in the middle helps to draw blood from the head above and the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it is composed of basilica and cephalic parts, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the surgeon must warn himself about the nerve that is underneath, and if it is not too deep, he finds the nerve
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and he inflates [the joint] and the patient suffers injury, and perhaps cannot recover
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	This nerve opens up very often, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you must heal it with the anesthesia tool; and follow the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is space between the two nerves, make an incision along it
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The surgery of the cephalic [bone] helps to draw blood from the head, and aids healing as well
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and one must operate by gripping the olive-shaped or mirt-shaped flame, for that is the safest of all the spaces because it does not have any nerve or artery underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one should try to find the easiest place [to operate], and do not harm anything if one fails at first; then one can begin again
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the site may swell in some people when it is operated upon incorrectly at first, but it does no harm
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the surgery depends on your skill.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about surgery is that it was invented only to preserve health
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future illnesses
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let surgery be done in one of the three spaces that are found there: namely, the cephalic, the fastigium, and the basilar
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should operate at the beginning of springtime, and in autumn and winter after meals, when the sign ofpletion appears
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should operate on the first or third day, after two or three hours from dawn.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The surgery that is performed for illnesses has no fixed time; but when there is need of it, it can be done at any hour and at all times
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one should not operate on children under fourteen years old, nor on women during the first four months of pregnancy up to seven months
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one operate on the elderly who have passed sixty years of age
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to undergo surgery in any way, they should cleanse their bowels with a light suppository
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw the impurities from the intestines to harm the main members
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one operate on those who are too fond of meat, nor those who are drunk at that time, nor dropsical people
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should avoid operating after a bout of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, menstruation in women, hard labor, excessive vigilance or fasting, and those who are completely without virtue, or who have been struck by a weapon or disease
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then refine the humors if the blood is thick, with foods and drinks and medications, if you are able to do so
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then take a bath if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and operate in the space around the third rib on the side of the chest, as we have said
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and on that day avoid work, food, and sexual intercourse, etc.;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be calm and cheerful, and let the surgeon be taller than the patient, and let them wipe their hands twice or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then strain the linen moderately above, for when it is too tight or short, blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the joint with both hands until you can feel the veins swell under them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then let him moisten the flame of a small piece of old oil with water, then place his left hand's thumb on that vein below where he wishes to cauterize.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Ensure that the vein does not bulge or swell when cauterizing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	Because there are veins that flee like cords to the sinew, and there are some that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Therefore, when one places heat on it, it retreats from the heat and cannot open the vein; thus are some of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	But if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be skilled in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first try, that is good; but if not, then restart a little lower or higher, as long as the area is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is inflamed and the patient is afraid, let it be for one or two days without tying the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for perhaps some swelling will come about; do not enter into a bath, then restart the surgery if he wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small or the skin covers it finely and you doubt that there is not much blood issuing from it, then apply all the heat directly to that opening itself;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and open it quickly before the area becomes inflamed; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area becoming inflamed, do not restart the surgery and apply a little oil mixed with lye, for it lightens the body's blood and is gentle in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the oil-and-lye mixture in every surgery that you perform on veins to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same remedy makes thrice and bowels of those who place it on the area; for it subtly draws out the blood and disperses it when it is too abundant.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large swelling comes about, which happens often, especially when the vein is not opened far enough during that first attempt where the opening of the vein was small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and apply a sponge moistened in warm water mixed with salt to the area, and leave it on for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the blood has issued from the vein, and if there remains afterward some blackness or greenness on the area for a few days, it will not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see that there is still something remaining, apply something of aloe or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is swelling and appearance of inflammation at the time of surgery like that of the basilisk: therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the area soft under the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to apply any of the remedies we have mentioned, for perhaps blood would flow from the artery; but instead make one dry dressing to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw off blood according to its quantity and according to its color.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it is thick, let it flow until it becomes thinned; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And he who is full and fat, and has need of bloodletting, should have a larger wound made for him, and the opening should be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and he who is weak should have the opposite done to him: let him be bled but little and often, and he must be bled in cutting across, not in pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bloodletting saves from loss of blood and injury to nerves, and is better than that done with a long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to him whose body fails during bloodletting, it is necessary to give bread moistened in juice of pomegranates; if he is overheated, let him have blood drawn three or four times
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold temperament, let him eat before bloodletting bread moistened in musk syrup or in spiced honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints during bloodletting after much blood has flowed, it is necessary that he inhale broth of meat and a subtle, fragrant syrup
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other remedies that we have mentioned in the chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to empty the arm vein and be bled again later, it is necessary that when he is weakened by much bloodletting, he be bled little by little according to his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to empty the arm vein after the first bloodletting and has a strong body, should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to have blood drawn from another vein should be bled on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood in the body that has already been heated and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw off a great quantity of it and widen the opening so that it flows freely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then when you have completed all the conditions for bloodletting and placed your hand on the pulse while bleeding, make sure that the mouth does not come in place of the opening
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens often if the bloodletter is careless.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And do not do this when you see that the arm has been untied and blood is flowing for the second time, and if the opening is closed, then press strongly upon it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, let him straighten his arm quickly, for that would be bad
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it flow until he bleeds the second time; or prick at the point of the opening until the frozen blood from the vein's mouth flows out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And apply a little salt mixed with water and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not squeeze it until the inflammation has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a necessity to draw blood a second time, do so in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are bled in place of the head vein because they are connected.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bloodletting is that the patient puts his hand into warm water until the veins become red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then let it be tied moderately so that the veins appear well, then bleed now across, not widely or deeply;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and bleed well near the joint of the hand; and if blood cannot flow out, put the hand back into warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in summer, do not put the hand back into warm water, for one puts it there more often in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And bloodletting from this vein is safer than from any other veins, because neither artery nor nerve is present there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	Bloodletting from the vein of the little finger of the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it should be done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Stretch out the hand, and put it into warm water until the vein becomes swollen so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and bleed across, and if you cut all around it, nothing will be harmed.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, because the nerves are located underneath all the flesh
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	"Then immerse the hand in warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound, so that it may flow out."
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And once you have cleaned off as much blood as necessary, then place a bandage of oil and flax to quickly bind the wound, and do this for each wound."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The swelling in the left hand is attributed to mouse disease, so perform the same treatment as I have instructed for the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	"The application of heat cautery is beneficial for all illnesses located beneath the body."
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	"such as diseases of the uterus, retention of urine, disease of the spine, and old diseases of the thighs and legs, and similar illnesses."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	"And the quality of its cautery is that the patient puts their foot in warm water, and rubs the wound until it reddens,"
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	"and then places it on the ankle joint; and the wound is located at the ankle, and many veins run from there up into the foot;"
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	"therefore cauterize either the larger vein or at the ankle, whichever is more beneficial."
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	"And if you cauterize on the foot, beware of the nerves beneath it, and make the cautery like a cut; and let the flame be gentle."
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if the blood cannot flow out, then put the foot back in the water and allow the vein to drain well."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	"And if cauterization does not succeed on the first try, begin again a little higher up the second time, for the place is tender;"
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	"do not fear damaging nerves, as we have said, and do likewise for the other foot if necessary."
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle joint, and its cauterization benefits sciatica pain when it is due to hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	"And the method of its cauterization is that the patient enters a bath and then applies four cautery marks on the outer ankle while twisting;"
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	"for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then cauterize in any way you can, even by cutting across it."
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	"And it is better that you cut it, for the location is safe and the vein is very common in many people."
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	"And if you cannot find it, then cauterize any vein that opens on the back of the foot near the little toe, but beware of nerves."
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	"And keep bleeding until you see blood flowing, then untie the bandage, and apply cotton and tie it securely; now it is cauterized."
Des sainies de ventouse	"On cupping (ventouse)"
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	"Cupping vessels are made of horn, or earthenware, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: either by pricking to attract blood, or without pricking."
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	"And this cupping without pricking is done in two ways: either with fire (heated cups) or without fire (cold cups)."
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	"And cupping performed by pricking and extracting blood is done in fourteen locations on the body,"
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	"of which one is entirely on the head, and another is on the neck;"
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	"And two others are located on each side of the neck; and the cupping vessel under the chin."
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	"And cupping vessels are placed on the shoulders and over the ribs."
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	"And cups are placed on both arms, and on both legs."
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	"And the cupping glasses of two cheeks; and cupping does not draw blood, except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh."
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	"Therefore it does not weaken anyone, as is done with bleeding from veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	"And it should not be administered, neither in all cases nor without fire and without heat, in any disease that arises from excess, until the whole body is emptied."
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	"And if it becomes necessary to cup due to illness or by custom, we will administer it each hour at the beginning of the month or at the end, and in-between and at all times."
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	"For there are people who, when they need to be cupped, have heavy heads;"
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	"And others find that they suffer from excess and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness before the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	"And those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have an enlarged tongue, and cough up blood;"
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	"And there are some who dream, seeing much blood and wounds and dead people, and things of that nature."
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially if they occur during the month, we order cupping to be performed after three hours of the day."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	"The bleeding of the temple helps against headache ... that afflicts them, but it should not be done after evacuation of the whole body."
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	"And this cupping is in lieu of bloodletting from the temple,"
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	"and those of cold temperament or with phlegm should not use it, for it harms them greatly;"
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	"And therefore old people and those who have cold conditions in their heads should not use it."
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, so one must place the cupping vessel a little lower down to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	"Cupping on the neck is in lieu of bloodletting from the head and nape of the neck, and therefore it is especially beneficial for throat inflammation;"
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	"And it helps with breaking up the phlegm channel, cough, and excess;"
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	"and it should not be placed too tightly, for if it holds too firmly it can cause forgetfulness or harm to the stomach or heart."
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	"Cupping on both sides of the neck is beneficial for headaches, optic pain, migraines, strangulation, and toothache;"
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	"and it is in lieu of bloodletting from the nape of the neck; and you should tell the practitioner to press gently when placing it, so that he does not cut the artery or cause profuse bleeding."
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Cupping under the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, gum inflammation, and similar conditions that are in the mouth; it is in lieu of bloodletting from both lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"Cupping on the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses that come from heat and excess;"
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	"Cupping on the ribs is as effective as cupping with three hollows of the arm;"
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	"for it attracts blood from these large vessels;"
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	"And tell the practitioner not to place it too deeply, for the area is thin and has nerves and arteries underneath."
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	"A cupping vessel placed on the buttock is beneficial for hemorrhoids and lower abdomen diseases. The vessel should be large and made of brass to draw well; if it were too thin, it might break and cause large wounds."
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	"Cupping on the legs draws openly, for it attracts blood from the whole body and is beneficial for old back pains, sciatica, bladder inflammation, and it strengthens the flesh. It is in lieu of the two sophenes (groin muscles) and the two ankles, but it can also weaken the body with prolonged use and cause edema in various conditions."
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	"The method of applying the cupping vessel is as follows: first place it empty and suck gently but steadily. Then apply it quickly and move it evenly until you see the area turn red and swollen, and the skin becomes flushed. Then remove it and replace the vessels. Be cautious about the condition of the body, for some people have thin flesh and clear pores; in this case, one should strike only once and make wide but not too deep wounds. Suck gently."
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"If the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the blood is very dense, one must strike a third time. But if we wish to draw only a little blood, once will suffice."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	"And if we wish to draw much blood, then strike repeatedly. If the blood is dense, strike deeply, and the endpoint is when the heart is pierced suddenly;"
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	"And those with thick and hard skin and narrow pores should oil the area of the cupping vessels with aperitive and solvent oil:"
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	"If it is in summer, use violet oil, sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;"
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	"And if it is winter, use watercress oil, lily oil, chamomile oil, or similar."
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	"And if the excess blood is thick and cold, use myrrh oil, balsam oil, fennel oil, or similar."
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	"And those with tender flesh and wide pores should not use any oil;"
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	"but they should wash the area after cupping with rosewater, cold water, blackberry juice, pumpkin juice, or other similar substances."
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	"And those with excessive moisture should rise using hyssop water, myrtle water, sumac water, or similar substances."
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	"And those with thick excesses should rise using old wine, vinegar water, fennel or chamomile decoction, or similar substances;"
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	"But do not perform cupping before bathing or in the bath. It should be done one or two hours after bathing, and one should not sleep immediately afterwards;"
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	"And one must ensure that they are warm when being cupped and have cupping performed."
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	"Be cautious with those who are choleric and have thick, fiery blood;"
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	"They should consume cold substances such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce with hyssop, and similar foods;"
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	"And eat chickpeas, castrated male lamb meat, and moist meats."
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	"And those with cold complexion should consume honey syrup and moderate aromatic wine that is between old and new. They should eat little, and consume chickpeas, small birds, and pigeons."
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	"On the day they are cupped, they should drink more than they eat;"
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	"And sometimes give men triacle or musk before or after cupping to strengthen the main organs;"
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	"Thin out the blood, but those who are hot should not drink it."
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	"The cupping vessels placed without striking are those applied to the liver, spleen, stomach, podagra (gout), abdomen, back, and buttocks, as these areas do not tolerate being struck."
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	"And this is only done to attract blood from one area to another;"
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	"for example, we place them on the breasts when there is milk congestion to draw out the viscosity from that area. Similarly, we apply cupping vessels to the abdomen and back to reduce the size of those areas."
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	"And relieves pain when there is retention or stone, so relieves by its attractive power perhaps the retention, or dislodges the stone from its place."
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	"And thus it does when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind."
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cups are administered empty for merely sucking; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of warm water
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	like in the case of diseases of the pleura, and in such manner that one fills the cup with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of administering the cupping glass with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be two digits wide and half a palm deep, and have on its circumference around the middle one small hole, just like for putting in a needle
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of earthenware, smooth beforehand so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in its middle a crossbar of earthenware or iron for placing an incense candle
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cups for children are different from those for adults, and those for thin people are different from those for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus place this cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	place the lit candle or one wick of flax into the cup through the crossbar that is inside the cup
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup and does not burn the patient
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, with both hands over the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wants to remove it, steam comes out and the cup is removed
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take away the wick as before, and repeat this often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Therefore, in the cupping glass used for diseases of the pleura, there is no crossbar or hole, and it is not administered with fire except when it is full of water. It is placed on the limb alone.
et c’est li forme:	And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups are not applied except in limbs where it is impossible to place them due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in places devoid of flesh, like the knees or toes, and other similar places.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	"and the qualities of urine are such that when you find it without sediment which are in clear sweet waters without corruption, then take it."
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	"And put them in fresh water until they become accustomed [to their surroundings], and have nothing in their bellies;"
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	"Then let there be a letting of blood and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and apply warm compresses."
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	"And once they are full [with blood], if they fall out and it is a place where cupping can be applied, apply the cupping glass, for this is very helpful."
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not so, then raise the joint gently, then with water, very well, and then compress it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	If the joint swells too much after the body of the shoulder blade, then soak one linen cloth in cold water and apply it until the swelling is reduced.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	If the swelling increases, apply ground vitriol or salt or similar substances until it subsides;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Alternatively, place half a handful of peeled fava beans on the joint and leave them there until they heat up; this will now stop the swelling.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other shoulder blades.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	If the shoulder blades do not stick, rub fresh blood on the joint and insert a needle there until the shoulder blade comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then apply them, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are attached, sprinkle a little powder of ground aloe and salt or ash on them so that they will stick firmly.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and provides treatment for broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians neglect this chapter, having never seen any of the ancient books or read a single letter from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, knowledge is lacking in our land, because I never found anyone skilled in it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	"And I know nothing except through the wisdom of old books which I have studied so much that I have treated their knowledge, and through experience, and through the habit of my life."
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	"And I have already described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the shapes of the tools that are arranged, as I did in these two preceding chapters."
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and chapters where the wise places his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are tried may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	"I say that when a breakage or dislocation or torsion or fracture comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick on one side and the other, if nothing prevents you from doing so, such as weakness of body, or childhood, or old age."
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	"or if the time is not very warm or too cold; and avoid eating cold things, that is to say cold foods, and poultry and venison, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have some doubt about an inflamed boil, or an expansion of matter in the limb; then the sick person should return to their usual regimen."
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the sick person with foods that promote growth and have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pears, and veal, eggs, fresh fish, and similar things, and strong wine."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment the wound will close more quickly and completely."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	"And know that the bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well restored nor healed according to their nature due to weakness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children."
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	"But do not hesitate to bind around the broken bone a thick cloth that fits and joins the limb together until it becomes strong again; and do not remove the splint too soon, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish them with fatty foods as we have said."
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that breaks are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For a break of the head is different from a break of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways that bones can break."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"For there are breaks that happen suddenly, and others that occur gradually, such as when cutting a feather to make a writing pen."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there is also breakage with wounding, and breaking with just a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	"And each type of break has its own method and appropriate tool for restoration, according to where the memory comes into play;"
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	"And a bone break is recognized by the twisted appearance of the site, and it is evident upon examination, and sounds hollow when pressed with the hand."
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	"And when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the sick person does not feel much pain, then there is no break."
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	"But it can still have twisting, cracking, or a small fracture."
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb by hand, but apply the medications that come later and then gently immobilize it."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	"And know that sudden breaks where the two parts are separated must be aligned equally before any inflammation appears;"
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	"and if inflammation does appear, allow it a few days to settle down until the inflammation is calmed;"
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	"then align the limb gently and straight, and know that this restoration is easier than those where there are pieces missing; then immobilize it as explained later."
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	"And if the bone has pieces broken off, then extend it from two points, whether it is an arm or leg, or use your hand for smaller limbs, or use two cords or one cord and your hand;"
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	"and align the limb according to its natural shape so that when the broken parts are separated, carefully fit the pieces back together using all your skill without causing injury or pain to the sick person;"
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	"And join the two ends of the bone together in the best alignment."
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"And you can feel with your hand whether it is well aligned or not: if not, realign it carefully and do not immobilize too tightly nor press in such a way that heat and stiffness are caused in the limb due to poor technique, as we have said many times before."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	"And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient to keep it still while awake or asleep, turning or in any other way;"
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	"and make sure that the limb is secured so that the patient feels no pain."
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	"For if there is any pain, then it is not properly aligned, and the limb must be positioned differently so that there is no pain;"
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	"And make sure that it is properly aligned so that no twisting occurs during healing."
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	"The quality of the bone fracture depends on what I have told you."
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken limbs are diverse in size, shape, and thickness."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	"There are small members such as arms and legs and similar ones: they should be wrapped with soft and fine linen bandages;"
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	"And those that are thick, such as thighs and legs, should be wrapped with wide and strong linen; for wide linen embraces the whole limb equally and immobilizes it without causing any indentation."
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	"Then wrap it with light bandages, three or four turns according to the limb size, and tighten your hand a little around all the linen; then go above the fracture and tie less tightly so that the fracture can move a little;"
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	"and loosen the linen a bit and a bit until you grasp most of the healthy area; then take another bandage and wrap it again over the broken area;"
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	"then go back to the area below the fracture and tie it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first section;"
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	"then place linen bandages or cloth between the layers of linen until it is all even; then tie everything together with one bandage from above, and then place your well-made splints on top if there is no inflammation or swelling."
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	"And if there is inflammation or heat, apply something cooling and anti-inflammatory, and let it be like that for a few days;"
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	"then immobilize your splints and make them half the width of a thick reed or use wood for fence posts or palm ribs, cut to this shape:"
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	"But the splint placed over the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others;"
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	"And it should also be long enough to suit the size of the limb."
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	"Then tie everything together again as you did in the first layer; then wrap it with thread in the same way as in the first layer over the fracture."
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	"Tie it tighter above and looser below; make sure that the thread is medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;"
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	If the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their knots with twisted linen cords, this is a great error; for the knot cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two inches between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is injured by the edges of the stakes after stretching in safe places, then place pads of linen or woolen gauze beneath them so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is accompanied by fracture and the bone is broken, I will describe its treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to stretch all broken limbs with stakes on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	Since limbs are large, do not place hot irons on them except after five or six days, or more according to your certainty of the heat of the inflammation occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the manner of the ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs; place this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, on the area where you will use it. This is the common way to make a plaster for restoring fractures in various conditions, especially for women and young children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make plaster for healing fractures and dislocations and torsions: Take bdellium, ladanum, lavender, asafetida, gum arabic, and mastic powder (each .x. ounces); myrrh and aloes (each .v. ounces); and aloe wood (.viiij. ounces). Grind these into a fine powder and mix it with plenty of eggs. If the person's constitution is hot, use this plaster because it has a good composition and quickly heals broken bones; useful for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make plaster that is useful for sprains: Take mastic and vitriol (each .x. ounces); myrrh and aloes (each .viiij. ounces); gum acacia (.vi. ounces); and bolic armenic (.x. ounces). Grind these ingredients well, then mix with water or plenty of eggs, and apply the mixture.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way to make plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their sockets, to relieve pain and reduce swelling, and to heal fractures: Take new linen, moisten it in warm water mixed with hot oil, and place it on the affected area. This plaster does not restore, but it is good for relieving heat from inflammation and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method to reset broken bones: Take dry fig leaves, and leaves of earth dock, grind together, make poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of poultice for the setting of broken bones and to facilitate the removal of bruises. Take root of mallow, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, each one part; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is hot, mix with coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of poultice stronger than the first one for setting broken bones with hard bruises. Take roots of mallow, linseed, almond, melilot, and comfrey, violet flowers and camomile flowers, each one part; grind and mix with salt water or fresh water or with wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not apply anything to the broken limb for setting besides wax and oil ointment, and nothing else more. He also says that it should be of medium consistency, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen believes that one should apply dry and slightly warm things to the broken limb for setting, such as myrrh, aloe, frankincense and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another poultice recipe for wounds and pain: Take mugwort and chopped horsehair or chicken feathers, mallow, and grind them equally. Make a poultice with the resulting mixture and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then remove the poultice after a while, being careful that the patient does not feel any pain and that the bone has not moved from its place. Do not remove it for too many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the place, with restlessness or swelling, be quick to remove the poultice and poultice remover. Take a light cloth, damp sea sponge, dip it in water and wipe the place until the itching stops and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	"Then allow the limb to rest for an hour, then place on it a dry linen cloth soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it tightly until you are sure of a hot abscess."
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be relieved, then resume the gentle binding, adding a little poultice, but do not bind it as tightly as before; continue gently until it is healed."
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	"And if you see that the abscess is hot and red, and there is pain and swelling, then you must resume binding it with poultice, just as you did initially."
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	"And if the limb does not improve with what we have said, do not untie it until after three days or four, five, or seven days; sometimes leave it tied for twenty days, according to how one sees that the fracture has healed and that the union of flesh is approaching."
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	"Then bind it more tightly than before, and the flesh will grow thicker, as I said earlier. But if you see that the area is drying out excessively, know that healing cannot occur there."
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	"Then apply warm water compresses every time you untie it, and do this every third day, loosening the bandage a little."
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	"Thus the healing of the limb is encouraged by this treatment, and quickly remedies what foolish physicians do, who reset a limb incorrectly. This is wicked, and such practices are weak; I see no other way than to leave it alone and operate correctly."
des diverses manieres de brisure	"Concerning the different kinds of fractures"
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	"There are many ways that bones can be fractured, with diverse appearances, and their causes are distinct."
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	"Some fractures are caused by a blow from a sword, which cuts through the bone all the way to its marrow, like splitting wood. This type of fracture is called 'haichure'."
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone without piercing it, that manner of fracture is called "absolute," and wounds from these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	"And if there is an embedded fracture, or a break from falling on stones, or from stones falling, or from similar causes."
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	"And if there is an open fracture that approaches the bone marrow, whether it is below or above the bone, this wound is either large or small."
